###begin article-title 0
###xml 81 83 81 83 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
CDPKs CPK6 and CPK3 Function in ABA Regulation of Guard Cell S-Type Anion- and Ca2+- Permeable Channels and Stomatal Closure
###end article-title 0
###begin article-title 1
Protein Kinases and Plant Pores
###end article-title 1
###begin p 2
###xml 81 83 81 83 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 152 154 152 154 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 267 269 267 269 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 491 507 491 507 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis CDPK</italic>
###xml 621 632 621 632 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis</italic>
###xml 654 658 654 658 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CDPK</italic>
###xml 666 670 666 670 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK3</italic>
###xml 675 679 675 679 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK6</italic>
###xml 726 728 726 728 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 824 826 824 826 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 904 912 904 912 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 957 959 957 959 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1018 1026 1018 1026 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 1237 1239 1237 1239 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1280 1282 1280 1282 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1375 1377 1375 1377 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1503 1505 1503 1505 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
Abscisic acid (ABA) signal transduction has been proposed to utilize cytosolic Ca2+ in guard cell ion channel regulation. However, genetic mutants in Ca2+ sensors that impair guard cell or plant ion channel signaling responses have not been identified, and whether Ca2+-independent ABA signaling mechanisms suffice for a full response remains unclear. Calcium-dependent protein kinases (CDPKs) have been proposed to contribute to central signal transduction responses in plants. However, no Arabidopsis CDPK gene disruption mutant phenotype has been reported to date, likely due to overlapping redundancies in CDPKs. Two Arabidopsis guard cell-expressed CDPK genes, CPK3 and CPK6, showed gene disruption phenotypes. ABA and Ca2+ activation of slow-type anion channels and, interestingly, ABA activation of plasma membrane Ca2+-permeable channels were impaired in independent alleles of single and double cpk3cpk6 mutant guard cells. Furthermore, ABA- and Ca2+-induced stomatal closing were partially impaired in these cpk3cpk6 mutant alleles. However, rapid-type anion channel current activity was not affected, consistent with the partial stomatal closing response in double mutants via a proposed branched signaling network. Imposed Ca2+ oscillation experiments revealed that Ca2+-reactive stomatal closure was reduced in CDPK double mutant plants. However, long-lasting Ca2+-programmed stomatal closure was not impaired, providing genetic evidence for a functional separation of these two modes of Ca2+-induced stomatal closing. Our findings show important functions of the CPK6 and CPK3 CDPKs in guard cell ion channel regulation and provide genetic evidence for calcium sensors that transduce stomatal ABA signaling.
###end p 2
###begin p 3
###xml 3 7 3 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CDPK</italic>
###xml 43 54 43 54 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis</italic>
TwoCDPK genes were found to be expressed inArabidopsis guard cells, where they are involved in ion channel regulation in response to abscisic acid signaling.
###end p 3
###begin title 4
Introduction
###end title 4
###begin p 5
###xml 283 284 283 284 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 378 379 378 379 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b001">1</xref>
###xml 380 381 380 381 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b003">3</xref>
###xml 536 537 536 537 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b001">1</xref>
###xml 538 539 538 539 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b004">4</xref>
###xml 621 623 621 623 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 642 644 642 644 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 645 648 645 648 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt</sub>
###xml 663 665 663 665 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 666 669 666 669 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt</sub>
###xml 719 720 719 720 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b005">5</xref>
###xml 721 722 721 722 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b009">9</xref>
###xml 761 763 761 763 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 808 810 808 810 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b010">10</xref>
###xml 811 813 811 813 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b011">11</xref>
Stomatal pores in the epidermis of aerial parts of plants facilitate gas exchange between plants and the atmosphere. Stomatal pores are surrounded by pairs of guard cells that mediate stomatal pore opening and closing. Guard cells respond to diverse stimuli, including blue light, CO2 concentrations, drought, pathogen attack, and plant hormones, including abscisic acid (ABA) [1-3]. Stomatal movements are mediated by ion transport across the plasma membrane and vacuolar membrane of guard cells and by organic solute content changes [1,4]. Guard cell ion channels and proton pumps are regulated by the cytosolic free Ca2+ concentration ([Ca2+]cyt) such that [Ca2+]cyt elevation activates stomatal closing mechanisms [5-9]. These findings correlate with the Ca2+ dependence of ABA-induced stomatal closing [10,11].
###end p 5
###begin p 6
###xml 59 61 59 61 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 62 65 62 65 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt</sub>
###xml 93 95 93 95 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b012">12</xref>
###xml 96 98 96 98 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b018">18</xref>
###xml 117 119 117 119 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b019">19</xref>
###xml 120 122 120 122 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b020">20</xref>
###xml 128 130 128 130 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 131 134 131 134 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt</sub>
###xml 234 235 234 235 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 301 302 301 302 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b005">5</xref>
###xml 303 304 303 304 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b007">7</xref>
###xml 305 307 305 307 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b016">16</xref>
###xml 308 310 308 310 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b021">21</xref>
###xml 351 352 351 352 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 428 430 428 430 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 578 580 578 580 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 620 622 620 622 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b022">22</xref>
###xml 623 625 623 625 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b024">24</xref>
###xml 714 716 714 716 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 749 751 749 751 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 791 793 791 793 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b025">25</xref>
###xml 810 811 810 811 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b003">3</xref>
###xml 812 813 812 813 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b004">4</xref>
###xml 820 830 820 830 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s3">Discussion</xref>
###xml 843 845 843 845 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1004 1006 1004 1006 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1130 1132 1130 1132 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1205 1240 1205 1240 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SOS3-like calcium binding protein 5</italic>
###xml 1242 1248 1242 1248 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SCaBP5</italic>
###xml 1250 1278 1250 1278 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Calcineurin B-like protein 1</italic>
###xml 1280 1284 1280 1284 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CBL1</italic>
###xml 1290 1294 1290 1294 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CBL9</italic>
###xml 1434 1436 1434 1436 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b026">26</xref>
###xml 1437 1439 1437 1439 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b027">27</xref>
###xml 1471 1473 1471 1473 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
ABA is a drought-inducible plant hormone. ABA regulates [Ca2+]cyt elevations in guard cells [12-18] and other cells [19,20]. [Ca2+]cyt elevation activates slow-type (S-type) anion efflux channels and down-regulates inward-rectifying K+ channels and proton pumps in the plasma membrane of guard cells [5,7,16,21]. The concomitant efflux of anions and K+ from guard cells results in turgor reduction and stomatal closure. Thus, Ca2+ elevation shifts ionic conductance properties in guard cells toward a stomatal closing favoring mode. Other studies indicate a possible role for Ca2+ in mediating stomatal opening as well [22-24]. It is noteworthy that ABA signal transduction in guard cells consists of not only a Ca2+-dependent response but also a Ca2+-independent possibly parallel pathway [25] (for reviews: [3,4], see Discussion). Whether Ca2+-independent mechanisms suffice for mediating full physiological stomatal ABA responses remains unclear. Genes encoding signal transduction proteins in both Ca2+-dependent and -independent pathways are still largely unknown and molecular genetic evidence for a rate-limiting role of Ca2+ as a positive transducer of ABA signaling is lacking. Repression of the SOS3-like calcium binding protein 5 (SCaBP5)/Calcineurin B-like protein 1 (CBL1) and CBL9 genes result in ABA hypersensitivity, suggesting that CBL1 and CBL9 function as negative regulators of an ABA signal transduction pathway [26,27]. However, no genes encoding Ca2+-sensing proteins that function as positive transducers of ABA signaling and of ion channel regulation in guard cells have been identified.
###end p 6
###begin p 7
###xml 28 30 28 30 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 31 34 31 34 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt</sub>
###xml 62 64 62 64 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b012">12</xref>
###xml 65 67 65 67 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b015">15</xref>
###xml 68 70 68 70 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b017">17</xref>
###xml 71 73 71 73 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b028">28</xref>
###xml 74 76 74 76 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b029">29</xref>
###xml 106 108 106 108 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 109 112 109 112 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt</sub>
###xml 155 157 155 157 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 207 209 207 209 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 269 271 269 271 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 339 341 339 341 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 375 377 375 377 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b029">29</xref>
###xml 399 401 399 401 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 443 445 443 445 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 499 501 499 501 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 521 523 521 523 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b029">29</xref>
###xml 524 526 524 526 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b031">31</xref>
###xml 555 557 555 557 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 617 619 617 619 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 620 623 620 623 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt</sub>
###xml 694 696 694 696 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b016">16</xref>
###xml 697 699 697 699 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b032">32</xref>
###xml 753 755 753 755 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 756 759 756 759 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt</sub>
###xml 856 858 856 858 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b033">33</xref>
ABA regulates repetitive [Ca2+]cyt elevations in guard cells [12-15,17,28,29]. Experimentally imposing [Ca2+]cyt transients revealed two distinguishable Ca2+-dependent stomatal closing responses: a rapid "Ca2+-reactive" stomatal closing response, and a long-lasting "Ca2+-programmed" stomatal closing response, which prevails even after Ca2+ transients have been terminated [29]. The long-lasting Ca2+-programmed response, but not the rapid Ca2+-reactive stomatal closing response, depends on the Ca2+ transient pattern [29-31]. However, the underlying Ca2+ transduction mechanisms remain unknown. In guard cells, [Ca2+]cyt elevation activates S-type anion channels via phosphorylation events [16,32], suggesting a role for phosphorylation events in [Ca2+]cyt signaling. We hypothesized that guard cell-expressed calcium-dependent protein kinases (CDPKs) [33] may function in transducing specific components of guard cell signal transduction and ion channel regulation.
###end p 7
###begin p 8
###xml 77 79 77 79 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b034">34</xref>
###xml 80 82 80 82 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b035">35</xref>
###xml 172 182 172 182 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Plasmodium</italic>
###xml 184 186 184 186 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b034">34</xref>
###xml 218 220 218 220 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 259 261 259 261 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 277 279 277 279 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b033">33</xref>
###xml 383 385 383 385 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 386 389 386 389 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt</sub>
###xml 452 454 452 454 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b033">33</xref>
###xml 455 457 455 457 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b034">34</xref>
###xml 556 558 556 558 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b036">36</xref>
###xml 608 621 608 621 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK10/AtCDPK1</italic>
###xml 623 634 623 634 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis</italic>
###xml 682 696 682 696 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK30/AtCDPK1a</italic>
###xml 754 756 754 756 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b037">37</xref>
###xml 813 820 813 820 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Petunia</italic>
###xml 822 824 822 824 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b038">38</xref>
###xml 863 882 863 882 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Medicago truncatula</named-content>
###xml 945 947 945 947 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b039">39</xref>
###xml 954 956 954 956 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1043 1044 1043 1044 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1070 1072 1070 1072 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b040">40</xref>
###xml 1090 1101 1090 1101 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis</italic>
###xml 1119 1120 1119 1120 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1140 1150 1140 1150 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Vicia faba</named-content>
###xml 1161 1163 1161 1163 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b041">41</xref>
###xml 1291 1293 1291 1293 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b036">36</xref>
###xml 1294 1296 1294 1296 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b037">37</xref>
###xml 1297 1299 1297 1299 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b041">41</xref>
###xml 1300 1302 1300 1302 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b050">50</xref>
###xml 1371 1382 1371 1382 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis</italic>
###xml 1455 1459 1455 1459 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CDPK</italic>
###xml 529 536 <span type="species:ncbi:4097">tobacco</span>
###xml 863 882 <span type="species:ncbi:3880">Medicago truncatula</span>
###xml 1140 1150 <span type="species:ncbi:3906">Vicia faba</span>
CDPKs are protein kinases that are broadly distributed in the plant kingdom [34,35]. In other kingdoms, CDPKs have been found only in certain groups of protists, including Plasmodium [34]. CDPKs contain an intrinsic Ca2+-activation domain with four EF hand Ca2+-binding sites [33]. CDPKs have been proposed to function in multiple plant signal transduction pathways downstream of [Ca2+]cyt elevations, thus transducing various physiological responses [33,34]. A virus-induced gene silencing study demonstrated a role of CDPKs in tobacco defense responses [36]. Dominant constitutively active mutant forms of CPK10/AtCDPK1 (Arabidopsis gene identifier number [AGI No.] At1g74740) or CPK30/AtCDPK1a (AGI No. At1g18890) cause constitutive stress signaling [37], dominant mutant isoforms affect pollen tube growth in Petunia [38], and antisense repression of CDPK in Medicago truncatula affected root hair development and the nodule formation rate [39]. A Ca2+-dependent kinase activity phosphorylates the guard cell-expressing inward-rectifying K+ channel, KAT1, in vitro [40] and recombinant Arabidopsis CDPK activates Cl- influx channels in Vicia faba vacuoles [41]. These results suggest functions of CDPKs in stomatal movements. Whereas many biochemical approaches show functions of CDPKs [36,37,41-50], gene disruption phenotypes of CDPKs have not yet been reported in Arabidopsis and would allow unequivocally pinpointing cellular functions of defined CDPK genes.
###end p 8
###begin p 9
###xml 44 55 44 55 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis</italic>
###xml 63 65 63 65 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b035">35</xref>
###xml 66 68 66 68 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b046">46</xref>
###xml 87 91 87 91 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CDPK</italic>
###xml 330 332 330 332 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b051">51</xref>
###xml 333 335 333 335 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b054">54</xref>
###xml 823 825 823 825 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b054">54</xref>
###xml 846 850 846 850 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CDPK</italic>
###xml 1024 1026 1024 1026 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1139 1141 1139 1141 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1167 1169 1167 1169 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1296 1298 1296 1298 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1392 1394 1392 1394 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
The CDPK gene family includes 34 members in Arabidopsis alone [35,46]. Redundancies in CDPK genes are likely to hamper molecular genetic analyses of CDPK functions. Recent studies have shown that relatively few signal transduction genes are expressed in a strictly cell-specific manner in roots, guard cells, and mesophyll cells [51-54]. However, signal transduction genes that are highly expressed in a given cell type, such as guard cells, are candidates for being incorporated into signal transduction networks within those cells. Furthermore, cell-specific signal transduction assays may allow resolution of phenotypes of single knockout mutants that global whole plant phenotypic analyses would not resolve in reverse genetic studies. Therefore, in the present study we used single cell-type gene expression analysis [54] to determine which CDPK genes are expressed in guard cells. We report phenotypes of loss-of-function mutants in two of the guard cell-expressed CDPKs and characterize functions of these CDPKs in Ca2+ activation of anion channels, in ABA activation of anion channels, and unexpectedly also in ABA regulation of Ca2+ channels as well as in Ca2+-reactive and ABA-induced stomatal closing. The presented results provide molecular genetic and cell biological evidence for Ca2+ sensors that function as positive transducers in plant ion channel regulation and ABA- and Ca2+-dependent signal transduction in guard cells.
###end p 9
###begin title 10
Results
###end title 10
###begin title 11
Expression of CDPK Genes
###end title 11
###begin p 12
###xml 13 17 13 17 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CDPK</italic>
###xml 31 42 31 42 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis</italic>
###xml 51 53 51 53 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b035">35</xref>
###xml 54 56 54 56 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b046">46</xref>
###xml 210 214 210 214 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CDPK</italic>
###xml 325 327 325 327 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b055">55</xref>
###xml 362 366 362 366 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CDPK</italic>
###xml 374 378 374 378 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK3</italic>
###xml 404 408 404 408 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK6</italic>
###xml 529 533 529 533 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK3</italic>
###xml 538 542 538 542 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK6</italic>
###xml 644 652 644 652 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 810 812 810 812 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b054">54</xref>
###xml 843 847 843 847 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK3</italic>
###xml 852 856 852 856 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK6</italic>
###xml 912 920 912 920 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 1041 1045 1041 1045 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">KAT1</italic>
###xml 1047 1055 1047 1055 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 1059 1061 1059 1061 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b056">56</xref>
###xml 1217 1220 1217 1220 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CBP</italic>
###xml 1337 1339 1337 1339 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b054">54</xref>
###xml 1345 1348 1345 1348 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CBP</italic>
###xml 1395 1403 1395 1403 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 1496 1500 1496 1500 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK3</italic>
###xml 1505 1509 1505 1509 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK6</italic>
###xml 1639 1641 1639 1641 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b054">54</xref>
###xml 1722 1726 1722 1726 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK3</italic>
###xml 1731 1735 1731 1735 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK6</italic>
There are 34 CDPK genes in the Arabidopsis genome [35,46]. To investigate whether and, if so, where CDPKs may function in ion channel regulation and guard cell signal transduction branches, we first identified CDPK genes expressed in guard cells using a guard cell-enriched cDNA library and RT-PCR with degenerate oligomers [55]. Two of the guard cell-expressed CDPK genes, CPK3 (AGI No.: At4g23650) and CPK6 (AGI No.: At2g17290), showed initial insertion mutant phenotypes and were therefore further analyzed. The expression of CPK3 and CPK6 in isolated guard cell protoplasts (GCPs) was further analyzed by RT-PCR with gene-specific primers (Figure 1A) and independently later by cell type-specific genomic scale expression analyses using Affymetrix (Santa Clara, California, United States) GeneChip assays [54]. RT-PCR analysis showed that CPK3 and CPK6 are expressed in both guard cells and mesophyll cells (Figure 1A). The purity of GCPs was analyzed by RT-PCR with specific primers for the guard cell-expressed potassium channel gene, KAT1 (Figure 1A) [56]. Guard cell preparations were further examined for contamination of mesophyll cells by analyzing mRNA abundance of a putative calmodulin-binding protein (CBP) (AGI No.: At4g33050), which was identified as being highly expressed in mesophyll cells but absent in guard cells [54]. No CBP mRNA was detected in guard cell preparations (Figure 1A), indicating that the GCP preparations had no or very little contamination. In addition to CPK3 and CPK6, several other CDPK genes were identified in guard cells by microarray experiments with guard cell RNA (Supplemental Table I in [54]). In this study, we focus on functional dissection of the guard cell-expressed CPK3 and CPK6 genes.
###end p 12
###begin p 13
###xml 128 132 128 132 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK3</italic>
###xml 137 141 137 141 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK6</italic>
###xml 204 206 204 206 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b057">57</xref>
###xml 292 298 292 298 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 314 320 314 320 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 336 342 336 342 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 362 368 362 368 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 442 448 442 448 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 453 459 453 459 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 531 539 531 539 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 560 566 560 566 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 666 672 666 672 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 697 705 697 705 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 882 886 882 886 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK3</italic>
###xml 890 894 890 894 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK6</italic>
###xml 916 922 916 922 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 927 933 927 933 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 995 1003 995 1003 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 1005 1006 1005 1006 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">.</italic>
###xml 1039 1045 1039 1045 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 1068 1074 1068 1074 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 1110 1118 1110 1118 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 1323 1324 1323 1324 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1331 1339 1331 1339 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 1439 1447 1439 1447 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 1453 1454 1453 1454 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g001">1</xref>
###xml 1500 1506 1500 1506 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 1533 1537 1533 1537 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK3</italic>
###xml 1549 1555 1549 1555 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 1565 1569 1565 1569 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK6</italic>
###xml 1581 1587 1581 1587 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3&#8211;1</italic>
To genetically analyze functions of CPK3 and CPK6 in guard cell signal transduction, we identified T-DNA insertion mutations in CPK3 and CPK6 from the Salk Institute Genomic Analysis Laboratory database [57]. Homozygous T-DNA insertion mutant lines were isolated and genomic sequences of the cpk3-1 (SALK_107620), cpk3-2 (SALK_022862), cpk6-1 (SALK_093308), and cpk6-2 (SALK_033392) insertion mutants were determined. The T-DNA insertions in cpk3-1 and cpk3-2 are localized in the first exon and in the first intron, respectively (Figure 1B). The insertion in cpk6-1 is localized in the second exon, 60 base-pairs downstream of the translation initiation codon, and cpk6-2 is in the first intron (Figure 1B). Southern blot analyses of homozygous plants indicated only a single band in each line, suggesting a single T-DNA insertion in these mutants (data not shown). Transcripts of CPK3 or CPK6 were not detected in cpk3-1 and cpk6-1 as demonstrated by RT-PCR utilizing whole leaf RNA extracts (Figure 1C). No RT-PCR band was observed for cpk3-2 (data not shown). For cpk6-2, no full-length cDNA was detected (Figure 1C). A faint band for transcript downstream of the T-DNA insertion was observed after 35 cycles of amplification showing substantially reduced mRNA levels (8% or less intensity compared to wild-type level, n = 2) (Figure 1C). Using a primer set in the first exon and the eighth exon, no RT-PCR amplification was observed (Figure 1B and 1C), showing that the first exon is missing in cpk6-2. We performed RT-PCR with CPK3 primers in cpk6-1 and with CPK6 primers in cpk3-1 to examine whether a compensatory expression occurs. No compensation in the wild-type transcript levels was observed (data not shown).
###end p 13
###begin p 14
###xml 11 15 11 15 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3</italic>
###xml 20 24 20 24 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6</italic>
###xml 36 48 36 48 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-1cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 53 65 53 65 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-2cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 174 205 174 205 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3&#8211;1, cpk3&#8211;2, cpk6&#8211;1, cpk6&#8211;2,</italic>
###xml 214 226 214 226 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-1cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 231 243 231 243 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-2cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 368 380 368 380 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-1cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 385 397 385 397 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-2cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
Homozygous cpk3 and cpk6 single and cpk3-1cpk6-1 and cpk3-2cpk6-2 double mutants were isolated and used for further analyses. Whole plant general morphological phenotypes of cpk3-1, cpk3-2, cpk6-1, cpk6-2, and the cpk3-1cpk6-1 and cpk3-2cpk6-2 double mutants were largely similar to wild-type plants (Columbia ecotype) under the standard growth conditions tested, but cpk3-1cpk6-1 and cpk3-2cpk6-2 double mutant plants showed a slight delay in growth by approximately 2 d in 4-wk-old plants compared to wild-type plants (data not shown).
###end p 14
###begin title 15
###xml 51 53 51 53 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 69 77 69 77 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
Activation of S-Type Anion Channels by Cytosolic Ca2+ Is Impaired in cpk3cpk6 Mutants
###end title 15
###begin p 16
###xml 183 184 183 184 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b005">5</xref>
###xml 185 186 185 186 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b009">9</xref>
###xml 187 189 187 189 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b016">16</xref>
###xml 190 192 190 192 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b032">32</xref>
###xml 193 195 193 195 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b055">55</xref>
###xml 196 198 196 198 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b058">58</xref>
###xml 199 201 199 201 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b062">62</xref>
###xml 313 315 313 315 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 366 371 366 371 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3,</italic>
###xml 376 380 376 380 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6</italic>
S-type anion efflux channels have been proposed to play an important role as targets of ABA signal transduction in guard cells and to be regulated by upstream phosphorylation events [5,9,16,32,55,58-62]. To determine whether CDPKs function in the activation of S-type anion channels in guard cells, we examined Ca2+ activation of S-type anion channels in wild-type, cpk3, and cpk6 single mutant and double mutant guard cells.
###end p 16
###begin p 17
###xml 18 26 18 26 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 45 47 45 47 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 48 51 48 51 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt</sub>
###xml 174 176 173 175 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 220 228 219 227 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 234 235 233 234 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g002">2</xref>
###xml 263 264 262 263 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b005">5</xref>
###xml 265 266 264 265 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b009">9</xref>
###xml 283 285 281 283 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 286 289 284 287 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt</sub>
###xml 371 372 369 370 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b009">9</xref>
###xml 433 435 430 432 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 436 439 433 436 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt</sub>
###xml 474 480 471 477 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 489 490 486 487 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 532 540 529 537 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 543 544 540 541 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 551 552 548 549 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 574 580 571 577 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 607 613 604 610 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 615 623 612 620 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 626 627 623 624 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 633 634 630 631 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 653 659 650 656 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 716 722 713 719 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 724 725 721 722 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 736 742 733 739 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 744 745 741 742 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 778 786 775 783 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 789 790 786 787 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 822 823 819 820 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 835 841 832 838 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 854 860 851 857 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 866 878 863 875 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-1cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 906 907 903 904 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1004 1012 1001 1009 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 1018 1019 1015 1016 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g002">2</xref>
###xml 1022 1023 1019 1020 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 1080 1092 1077 1089 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-2cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 1094 1102 1091 1099 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 1105 1106 1102 1103 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1112 1113 1109 1110 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 1132 1144 1129 1141 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-1cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 1221 1229 1218 1226 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 1235 1236 1232 1233 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g002">2</xref>
###xml 1276 1280 1273 1277 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK6</italic>
###xml 1305 1309 1302 1306 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK3</italic>
###xml 1328 1332 1325 1329 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK3</italic>
###xml 1337 1341 1334 1338 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK6</italic>
###xml 1362 1364 1359 1361 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
As illustrated in Figure 2, typical large [Ca2+]cyt-activated S-type anion channel currents were observed in wild-type guard cells in the presence of elevated (2 muM) free Ca2+ in the patch pipette (cytosolic) solution (Figure 2A and 2C) as previously described [5,9]. At 0.1 muM [Ca2+]cyt in the pipette, large S-type anion currents were not activated (data not shown) [9]. S-type anion channel currents in the presence of 2 muM [Ca2+]cyt were significantly reduced in the cpk3-1 mutant (n = 11 guard cells) compared to wild-type (Figure 2C; n = 17, p = 0.022 at -145 mV). cpk3-2 showed similar results to cpk3-1 (Figure 2C; n = 7, p > 0.4 compared to cpk3-1). S-type anion channel currents were further reduced in cpk6-1 (n = 11) and cpk6-2 (n = 4) single mutant guard cells (Figure 2C; p < 0.005 compared to wild-type; p > 0.18 for cpk6-1 compared to cpk6-2). In cpk3-1cpk6-1 double mutant guard cells (n = 17), S-type anion channel currents were substantially reduced compared to wild-type controls (Figure 2B and 2C; p < 0.0005). Essentially similar results were obtained in cpk3-2cpk6-2 (Figure 2C; n = 6, p > 0.4 compared to cpk3-1cpk6-1). Nevertheless, background anion currents did remain in the double mutants (Figure 2B and 2C). The data showed stronger effects of CPK6 disruptions compared to CPK3 disruptions. Thus CPK3 and CPK6 are important for Ca2+ activation of S-type anion channels.
###end p 17
###begin title 18
###xml 57 65 57 65 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
Impairment in ABA Activation of S-Type Anion Channels in cpk3cpk6 Mutants
###end title 18
###begin p 19
###xml 126 128 126 128 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 180 190 180 190 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s3">Discussion</xref>
###xml 206 207 206 207 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b003">3</xref>
###xml 208 209 208 209 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b004">4</xref>
###xml 381 389 381 389 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 413 415 413 415 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 484 505 484 505 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
###xml 508 509 508 509 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b009">9</xref>
###xml 524 532 524 532 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 591 593 591 593 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 613 615 612 614 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 711 719 710 718 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 822 830 821 829 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 833 834 832 833 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g003">3</xref>
###xml 845 846 844 845 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 856 868 855 867 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-1cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 870 871 869 870 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 881 893 880 892 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-2cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 895 896 894 895 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 983 991 982 990 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 994 995 993 994 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g003">3</xref>
###xml 1006 1007 1005 1006 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 1120 1121 1119 1120 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b003">3</xref>
###xml 1153 1155 1152 1154 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1227 1236 1226 1235 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g002">Figures 2</xref>
###xml 1241 1242 1240 1241 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g003">3</xref>
###xml 1368 1370 1366 1368 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1374 1382 1372 1380 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 1392 1400 1390 1398 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 1540 1542 1538 1540 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1603 1605 1601 1603 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1614 1616 1612 1614 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b063">63</xref>
Previous studies have shown that guard cell signal transduction is mediated by a network of events, which includes parallel Ca2+-dependent and -independent signaling branches (see Discussion; for reviews: [3,4]). Therefore, experiments were pursued to analyze ABA activation of S-type anion channels. These experiments were performed under different conditions than those shown in Figure 2, such that cytosolic Ca2+ elevation alone would not fully activate S-type anion currents (see Materials and Methods) [9]. As shown in Figure 3, with preincubation of guard cells in low extracellular Ca2+, 2 muM cytosolic Ca2+ in the pipette activated S-type anion currents in guard cells of only intermediate amplitudes (Figure 3A). Under these conditions, ABA up-regulated S-type anion current activities in wild-type protoplasts (Figure 3A, 3B, and 3E; n = 8). In cpk3-1cpk6-1 (n = 7) and cpk3-2cpk6-2 (n = 7) double mutant guard cells, ABA regulation of S-type anion currents was impaired (Figure 3C, 3D, and 3E; p < 0.01). These data show that, despite the complex network of ion channel regulation mechanisms in guard cells [3], CDPKs mediate an important Ca2+-decoding transduction step in ABA regulation of S-type anion channels (Figures 2 and 3). ABA activation in wild-type guard cells and the impairment in ABA activation of S-type anion channels at 2 muM cytosolic Ca2+ in cpk3cpk6 mutants (Figure 3) further provide evidence for a recently proposed hypothesis in which stomatal closing signals (i.e., ABA) mediate priming of guard cell Ca2+ sensors, such that they can respond to elevated cytosolic Ca2+ levels [63].
###end p 19
###begin title 20
###xml 33 35 33 35 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 48 57 48 57 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3 cpk6</italic>
Impairment in ABA activation of ICa Channels in cpk3 cpk6 Mutants
###end title 20
###begin p 21
###xml 32 34 32 34 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 47 49 47 49 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 61 63 61 63 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b064">64</xref>
###xml 64 66 64 66 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b066">66</xref>
###xml 158 160 158 160 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 257 258 257 258 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b009">9</xref>
###xml 259 261 259 261 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b053">53</xref>
###xml 262 264 262 264 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b064">64</xref>
###xml 265 267 265 267 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b066">66</xref>
###xml 290 294 290 294 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK3</italic>
###xml 299 303 299 303 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK6</italic>
###xml 335 337 335 337 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
ABA activates plasma membrane Ca2+-permeable (ICa) channels [64-66]. Combined physiological, molecular genetic, and cell biological analyses have shown that ICa channels function in the guard cell ABA signal transduction network at hyperpolarized voltages [9,53,64-66]. We examined whether CPK3 and CPK6 function in the regulation of ICa channels.
###end p 21
###begin p 22
###xml 9 11 9 11 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 112 120 112 120 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 126 127 126 127 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g004">4</xref>

###xml 221 233 221 233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-2cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
