###xml 271 272 271 272 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g004">4</xref>
###xml 275 276 275 276 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 283 284 283 284 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 296 308 296 308 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-1cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 310 311 310 311 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 317 318 317 318 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 330 342 330 342 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-2cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 471 472 471 472 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 492 493 492 493 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 502 514 502 514 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-1cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 640 642 640 642 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 655 663 655 663 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 767 769 767 769 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 814 816 814 816 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 847 853 847 853 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 855 861 855 861 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 863 870 863 870 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6&#8211;1,</italic>
###xml 875 881 875 881 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 898 906 898 906 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 908 909 908 909 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g004">4</xref>
###xml 912 913 912 913 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 919 920 919 920 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 932 938 932 938 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 940 941 940 941 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 948 949 948 949 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 961 967 961 967 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 969 970 969 970 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 976 977 976 977 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 989 995 989 995 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 997 998 997 998 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1004 1005 1004 1005 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 1017 1024 1017 1024 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6&#8211;2,</italic>
###xml 1103 1107 1103 1107 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK3</italic>
###xml 1112 1116 1112 1116 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK6</italic>
###xml 1148 1150 1148 1150 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 1161 1169 1161 1169 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 1177 1179 1177 1179 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1225 1234 1225 1234 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g002">Figures 2</xref>
###xml 1239 1240 1239 1240 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g003">3</xref>
Typical ICa currents were activated by extracellular application of ABA to patch-clamped wild-type guard cells (Figure 4A and 4B, n = 13). Unexpectedly, ABA activation of ICa channels was not observed in cpk3-1cpk6-1 and cpk3-2cpk6-2 double mutant guard cells (Figure 4C-4E; n = 14, p = 0.56 for cpk3-1cpk6-1; n = 8, p = 0.47 for cpk3-2cpk6-2 when comparing before and after ABA treatment). Blind patch-clamp experiments in which the genotype of protoplasts was unknown (n = 2 for wild-type, n = 2 for cpk3-1cpk6-1), and similar findings by Y.M., I.C.M., Y.W., and S.M. in this study, further confirmed the impairment of ABA activation of ICa channels in cpk3cpk6 mutant guard cells. Next we analyzed whether only one of the two CDPKs might affect ABA activation of ICa channels. Defects in the ABA activation of ICa channels were observed in the cpk3-1, cpk3-2, cpk6-1, and cpk6-2 single mutants (Figure 4F-4I; n = 9, p = 0.38 for cpk3-1; n = 11, p = 0.47 for cpk6-1; n = 3, p = 0.96 for cpk3-2; n = 5, p = 0.30 for cpk6-2, when comparing before and after ABA-treatment). Together these data show that CPK3 and CPK6 function in ABA regulation of ICa channels (Figure 4) and Ca2+ and ABA activation of S-type anion channels (Figures 2 and 3).
###end p 22
###begin p 23
###xml 154 156 154 156 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 183 194 183 194 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis</italic>
###xml 305 306 305 306 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">R</italic>
###xml 309 310 309 310 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S</italic>
###xml 314 315 314 315 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S</italic>
###xml 391 392 391 392 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H</italic>
###xml 394 395 394 395 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H</italic>
###xml 398 399 398 399 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">H</italic>
###xml 403 404 403 404 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">b</italic>
###xml 407 408 407 408 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a</italic>
###xml 423 426 423 426 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">a,g</italic>
###xml 438 443 438 443 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">c,d,e</italic>
###xml 858 860 858 860 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 901 902 901 902 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 991 993 990 992 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 1004 1012 1003 1011 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 1018 1019 1017 1018 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g004">4</xref>
###xml 1022 1023 1021 1022 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1029 1030 1028 1029 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 1098 1102 1097 1101 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3</italic>
###xml 1107 1111 1106 1110 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6</italic>
###xml 1144 1146 1143 1145 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 1283 1285 1282 1284 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 1296 1298 1295 1297 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b066">66</xref>
###xml 1340 1350 1339 1349 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s3">Discussion</xref>
To gain insight into the question whether activation of phosphorylation events are required before or after ABA application and during ABA activation of ICa channels in patch-clamped Arabidopsis guard cells, wild-type guard cells were pretreated with the broad serine/threonine kinase inhibitor, K252a [(8R*,9S*,11S*)-(-)-9-hydroxy-9-methoxycarbonyl-8-methyl-2,3,9,10-tetrahydro-8,11,epoxy-1H,8H,11H-2,7b,11a-triazadibenzo[a,g]cyclo-octa[c,d,e]-trinden-1-one], 20 min prior to, and continuously during, patch clamping. Moreover, the cytoplasm of whole cells was dialyzed in the absence of ATP in whole cell recordings for longer than 15 min prior to extracellular ABA exposure. Ionic currents were recorded in the same guard cells prior to and after exposure to ABA. In negative controls, treatment with K252a alone did not cause constitutive activation of ICa channel currents without ABA treatment (n = 3). Interestingly, pretreatment with K252a (2 muM) did not disrupt ABA activation of ICa channels (Figure 4J and 4K; n = 6, p < 0.04 at -180 mV). These findings indicate that the effect of the cpk3 and cpk6 mutations on ABA activation of ICa channel currents are most likely not caused by direct ABA-induced upstream CDPK activation in the NADPH-dependent activation branch of ICa channels [66], but possibly by prior CDPK action (see Discussion).
###end p 23
###begin p 24
###xml 61 63 61 63 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 142 144 142 144 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 197 201 197 201 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gca2</italic>
###xml 206 212 206 212 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">abi2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 214 216 214 216 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b065">65</xref>
###xml 217 219 217 219 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b066">66</xref>
###xml 234 242 234 242 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g005">Figure 5</xref>
###xml 277 279 277 279 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 305 313 305 313 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 355 363 355 363 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g005">Figure 5</xref>
###xml 365 366 365 366 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 372 373 372 373 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 386 398 386 398 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-1cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 400 401 400 401 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 407 408 407 408 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 420 433 420 433 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-2cpk6&#8211;2;</italic>
###xml 438 439 438 439 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 445 446 445 446 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 502 503 502 503 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 504 505 504 505 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
We further examined whether the defect in ABA activation of ICa channels is due to impairment in reactive oxygen species (ROS) activation of ICa channels, as found for the ABA-insensitive mutants, gca2 and abi2-1 [65,66]. As shown in Figure 5, hydrogen peroxide activation of ICa channels was observed in cpk3cpk6 double mutant and wild-type guard cells (Figure 5; n = 7, p < 0.001 for cpk3-1cpk6-1; n = 4, p < 0.05 for cpk3-2cpk6-2; and n = 7, p < 0.01 for wild-type; when comparing before and after H2O2 treatment).
###end p 24
###begin title 25
###xml 11 13 11 13 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
ABA- and Ca2+-Induced Stomatal Closure
###end title 25
###begin p 26
###xml 30 32 30 32 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 100 102 100 102 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 128 136 128 136 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 201 205 201 205 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cdpk</italic>
###xml 301 309 300 308 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g006">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 312 313 311 312 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 359 371 358 370 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-1cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 376 388 375 387 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-2cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 441 449 440 448 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g006">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 452 459 451 458 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0040327-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 461 462 460 461 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 508 509 506 507 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 521 533 519 531 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-1cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 552 553 550 551 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 584 585 582 583 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 598 610 596 608 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-2cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 692 696 690 694 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3</italic>
###xml 701 705 699 703 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6</italic>
###xml 729 730 727 728 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 740 747 738 745 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0040327-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 779 783 777 781 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK3</italic>
###xml 788 792 786 790 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK6</italic>
The findings that cytosolic Ca2+ and ABA activation of S-type anion channels and ABA activation of ICa channels are impaired in cpk3cpk6 mutants led us to examine ABA-induced stomatal closure in these cdpk mutants. Application of 1 and 10 muM ABA induced a decrease in stomatal aperture in wild-type (Figure 6A, n = 13 experiments, 260 stomata). In contrast, cpk3-1cpk6-1 and cpk3-2cpk6-2 double mutant stomata showed reduced ABA responses (Figure 6A, Table 1, n = 7 experiments, 140 stomata; at 10 muM ABA: p < 0.01 for cpk3-1cpk6-1 versus wild-type; n = 4 experiments, 120 stomata, p < 0.011 for cpk3-2cpk6-2). Furthermore, ABA-induced stomatal closing was partially impaired in all of the cpk3 and cpk6 single mutant alleles (p < 0.05) (Table 1). These results show roles for CPK3 and CPK6 in ABA-induced stomatal closure.
###end p 26
###begin p 27
###xml 16 18 16 18 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 83 85 83 85 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 113 115 113 115 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b067">67</xref>
###xml 116 118 116 118 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b069">69</xref>
###xml 148 149 147 148 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 193 201 192 200 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g006">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 221 233 220 232 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-1cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 238 250 237 249 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-2cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 349 357 348 356 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g006">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 360 361 359 360 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 373 385 372 384 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-1cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 390 391 389 390 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 403 415 402 414 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-2cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 438 440 436 438 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 454 456 452 454 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 512 516 510 514 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3</italic>
###xml 521 525 519 523 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6</italic>
###xml 542 543 540 541 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 565 566 563 564 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
Extracellular Ca2+ causes stomatal closing, by initiating repetitive cytoplasmic Ca2+ elevations in guard cells [67-69]. Application of 100 muM CaCl2 to intact leaves closed wild-type stomata (Figure 6B). However, in the cpk3-1cpk6-1 and cpk3-2cpk6-2 double mutants, stomatal closure was significantly attenuated compared to the wild-type response (Figure 6B, p < 0.01 for cpk3-1cpk6-1 and p < 0.05 for cpk3-2cpk6-2 at 100 muM external Ca2+). External Ca2+-induced stomatal closing was also impaired in all four cpk3 and cpk6 single mutants (n = 60 to 100 stomata; p < 0.05, data not shown).
###end p 27
###begin p 28
###xml 22 24 22 24 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 109 111 109 111 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 112 115 112 115 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt</sub>
###xml 152 160 152 160 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 183 185 183 185 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b029">29</xref>
###xml 186 188 186 188 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b031">31</xref>
###xml 189 191 189 191 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b068">68</xref>
###xml 198 200 198 200 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 296 316 296 316 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">long-term programmed</italic>
###xml 378 389 378 389 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis</italic>
###xml 391 393 391 393 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b029">29</xref>
###xml 456 458 456 458 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 556 558 556 558 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 656 658 656 658 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b029">29</xref>
###xml 720 722 720 722 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 754 775 754 775 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
###xml 780 782 780 782 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 863 865 863 865 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 882 894 882 894 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-1cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 939 947 939 947 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g007">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 994 996 994 996 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 997 1000 997 1000 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt</sub>
###xml 1042 1054 1042 1054 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-1cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 1082 1083 1082 1083 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 1141 1142 1139 1140 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1165 1177 1163 1175 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-1cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 1202 1203 1198 1199 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1209 1221 1205 1217 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-1cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 1268 1270 1264 1266 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1271 1274 1267 1270 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt</sub>
###xml 1363 1375 1359 1371 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-1cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 1389 1390 1385 1386 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 1440 1441 1434 1435 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1464 1476 1458 1470 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-1cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 1508 1509 1500 1501 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 1515 1527 1507 1519 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-1cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 1592 1594 1584 1586 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1606 1608 1598 1600 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1609 1612 1601 1604 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt</sub>
###xml 1663 1665 1655 1657 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1702 1704 1694 1696 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b067">67</xref>
###xml 1705 1707 1697 1699 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b069">69</xref>
To further evaluate Ca2+ regulation of stomatal closure, we examined the effect of experimentally imposed [Ca2+]cyt oscillations on stomatal closure in cpk3cpk6 double mutant plants [29-31,68]. A Ca2+ oscillation pattern was applied to guard cells with a similar time pattern to those that cause long-term programmed stomatal closure (i.e., inhibition of stomatal reopening) in Arabidopsis [29]. Hypothesizing a contribution of additional CDPKs or other Ca2+ transducers in these experiments, we applied a hyperpolarizing buffer with lower extracellular Ca2+ concentrations (1 mM) and higher KCl concentrations (1 mM) than those used in previous research [29] with the goal of experimentally imposing weaker cytosolic Ca2+ transients in guard cells (see Materials and Methods). Ca2+ imaging experiments of guard cells showed that this protocol causes cytosolic Ca2+ oscillations in cpk3-1cpk6-1 double mutant and in wild-type guard cells (Figure 7, inset). The average amplitudes of imposed [Ca2+]cyt transients were similar in wild-type and cpk3-1cpk6-1 double mutant guard cells (p = 0.25; wild-type: 0.725 ratio units [RU] +/- 0.043 SEM, n = 16 wild-type cells; cpk3-1cpk6-1: 0.766 RU +/- 0.04 SEM, n = 24 cpk3-1cpk6-1 guard cells). The average integrated total [Ca2+]cyt ratio increase per period was also determined and found to be similar for wild-type and cpk3-1cpk6-2 guard cells (p = 0.46; wild-type: 8.535 RU * 0.1 min +/- 0.497, n = 16 wild-type cells; cpk3-1cpk6-1: 8.456 RU * 0.1 min +/- 0.517, n = 24 cpk3-1cpk6-1 cells). These data are consistent with findings that external Ca2+-induced [Ca2+]cyt elevations in guard cells include intracellular Ca2+ release from guard cell organelles [67,69].
###end p 28

###xml 639 651 639 651 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-2cpk6&#8211;2</italic>

###xml 699 711 699 711 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-2cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 744 752 744 752 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 964 965 964 965 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 994 1002 994 1002 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g007">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 1072 1080 1072 1080 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 1158 1160 1158 1160 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1282 1294 1282 1294 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-1cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 1299 1311 1299 1311 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-2cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 1313 1314 1313 1314 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 1359 1361 1359 1361 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1424 1432 1424 1432 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 1473 1475 1473 1475 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1514 1516 1514 1516 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b029">29</xref>
###xml 1517 1519 1517 1519 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b031">31</xref>
###xml 1547 1555 1547 1555 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g007">Figure 7</xref>
Four Ca2+ transients with a 10-min period, which induce long-lasting "Ca-programmed" stomatal closure [29], were applied to wild-type and cpk3cpk6 double mutant stomata. Wild-type stomata started closing immediately after the first Ca2+ elevation was imposed and continued to show progressive Ca2+-reactive closing for longer than 40 min (Figure 7; n = 6 experiments, 47% closure). In contrast, Ca2+ transient-induced closure of cpk3-1cpk6-1 and cpk3-2cpk6-2 double mutant stomata was reduced (14% and 22 % closure, respectively) (Figure 7; n = 6 experiments, p < 0.01 for cpk3-1cpk6-1 versus wild-type and n = 3 experiments, p < 0.05 for cpk3-2cpk6-2 versus wild-type, p > 0.60 cpk3-1cpk6-1 versus cpk3-2cpk6-2). Stomata of both wild-type and cpk3cpk6 double mutant guard cells remained closed during the ensuing 2 h and 20 min measurements, even though cells were extracellularly bathed in a typical "stomatal opening" solution containing 50 mM KCl and 0 mM CaCl2 and exposed to white light (Figure 7, from 40 to 180 min). Interestingly, the partial stomatal closure of cpk3cpk6 double mutants was also maintained during the ensuing 2 h and 20 min after Ca2+ transients were terminated, i.e. a significant stomatal closure was observed at 180 min when compared with 0 min in both cpk3-1cpk6-1 and cpk3-2cpk6-2 (p < 0.01 for both mutants). Thus, the rapid Ca2+-reactive stomatal closure response is clearly impaired in the cpk3cpk6 double mutants, whereas the long-term Ca2+-programmed stomatal closure response [29-31] appears to be functional (Figure 7).
###end p 29
###begin p 30
###xml 67 79 67 79 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-1cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 84 96 84 96 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-2cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 198 206 198 206 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
Seed germination analyses were also pursued with wild-type and the cpk3-1cpk6-1 and cpk3-2cpk6-2 double mutants. No significant difference in ABA inhibition of seed germination in wild-type and the cpk3cpk6 double mutant alleles was observed in the presence of 0, 0.3, 1, and 5 muM ABA after 3, 5, 7, and 11 d (unpublished data).
###end p 30
###begin title 31
###xml 60 68 60 68 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
Rapid-Type Anion Channel Activity Is Not Greatly Altered in cpk3cpk6 Double Mutant
###end title 31
###begin p 32
###xml 116 118 116 118 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b062">62</xref>
###xml 119 121 119 121 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b070">70</xref>
###xml 122 124 122 124 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b073">73</xref>
###xml 212 220 212 220 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 234 242 234 242 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g008">Figure 8</xref>
###xml 308 316 308 316 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g008">Figure 8</xref>
###xml 322 333 322 333 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis</italic>
###xml 380 382 380 382 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 516 518 516 518 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b065">65</xref>
###xml 617 618 617 618 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 759 768 759 768 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g002">Figures 2</xref>
###xml 773 774 773 774 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g003">3</xref>
###xml 874 886 874 886 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-1cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 914 922 914 922 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g008">Figure 8</xref>
###xml 928 929 928 929 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g008">8</xref>
###xml 943 944 943 944 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 950 962 950 962 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-1cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 964 965 964 965 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>
###xml 971 972 971 972 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 1004 1012 1004 1012 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 1150 1158 1150 1158 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 1179 1187 1179 1187 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g006">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 1189 1196 1189 1196 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0040327-t001">Table 1</xref>
ABA also regulates a second class or mode of anion channels in guard cells, the rapid-type (R-type) anion channels [62,70-73]. Therefore, we also compared R-type anion channel current properties in wild-type and cpk3cpk6 guard cells (Figure 8). The selectivity for anions over cations of these ion currents (Figure 8A) in Arabidopsis guard cells was further analyzed. Replacing Ba2+ with the impermeable cation tetraethylamonium in the bath solution did not affect these R-type inward currents, as previously shown [65]. Moreover, use of the impermeable anion gluconate in the pipette solution abolished the current (n = 3, data not shown), confirming that the recorded currents are R-type anion currents. Interestingly, in contrast to S-type anion channels (Figures 2 and 3), no significant difference was observed in the rapid anion channel activity between wild-type and cpk3-1cpk6-1 double mutant guard cells (Figure 8A and 8B; wild-type, n = 7; cpk3-1cpk6-1, n = 7; p = 0.21 at peak current). Thus, cpk3cpk6 mutant guard cells did not significantly impair R-type anion currents, which correlated with the partial ABA-induced stomatal closing in cpk3cpk6 mutant guard cells (Figure 6, Table 1).
###end p 32
###begin title 33
Discussion
###end title 33
###begin p 34
###xml 67 69 67 69 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 124 126 124 126 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b033">33</xref>
###xml 127 129 127 129 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b034">34</xref>
###xml 205 207 205 207 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b036">36</xref>
###xml 208 210 208 210 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b040">40</xref>
###xml 211 213 211 213 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b041">41</xref>
###xml 214 216 214 216 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b043">43</xref>
###xml 217 219 217 219 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b045">45</xref>
###xml 220 222 220 222 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b048">48</xref>
###xml 223 225 223 225 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b050">50</xref>
###xml 226 228 226 228 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b074">74</xref>
###xml 256 258 256 258 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b037">37</xref>
###xml 294 296 294 296 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b049">49</xref>
###xml 391 395 391 395 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cdpk</italic>
###xml 473 475 473 475 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b036">36</xref>
###xml 505 524 505 524 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Medicago truncatula</named-content>
###xml 537 539 537 539 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b039">39</xref>
###xml 592 596 592 596 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CDPK</italic>
###xml 706 710 706 710 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CDPK</italic>
###xml 855 858 855 858 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk</italic>
###xml 464 471 <span type="species:ncbi:4097">tobacco</span>
###xml 505 524 <span type="species:ncbi:3880">Medicago truncatula</span>
CDPKs have been predicted to function in response to cytoplasmic Ca2+ elevations in many physiological processes in plants [33,34]. Many biochemical studies have suggested roles of CDPKs in plant biology [36,40,41,43,45,48-50,74]. A dominant mutant study [37] and a biochemical study of CPK32 [49] have provided evidence for functions of CDPKs in ABA signaling, and gene-silencing/antisense cdpk mutant phenotypes were demonstrated for a plant defense response in tobacco [36] and for nodule formation in Medicago truncatula root hairs [39]. The relative dearth of genetic or reverse genetic CDPK loss-of-function mutation phenotypes may be attributed to partial redundancies in the functions of the large CDPK gene family. Furthermore, cell-specific and mechanistic protein regulation (e.g., ion channel) analyses allow resolution of quantitative single cpk gene disruption mutant phenotypes, as demonstrated here.
###end p 34
###begin p 35
###xml 253 264 253 264 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis</italic>
###xml 316 318 316 318 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b052">52</xref>
###xml 319 321 319 321 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b054">54</xref>
###xml 431 433 431 433 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b075">75</xref>
###xml 727 729 727 729 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b055">55</xref>
###xml 730 732 730 732 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b076">76</xref>
###xml 733 735 733 735 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b079">79</xref>
###xml 751 753 751 753 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b080">80</xref>
###xml 997 999 997 999 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1092 1094 1092 1094 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1106 1108 1106 1108 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 424 429 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
Our findings do not exclude the possibility that the CDPKs analyzed here may function in other pathways in other plant tissues. Single cell-type microarray studies have shown that relatively few genes are expressed in a strictly cell-specific manner in Arabidopsis root cell types, guard cells, and mesophyll cells [52,54]. Combinatorial usage of a single protein in different signaling pathways was initially documented in yeast [75]. Furthermore, studies of mitogen-activated protein kinase and protein phosphatase genes in plants have suggested that individual mitogen-activated protein kinases and protein phosphatases function in different signal transduction cascades in different tissues and under different conditions [55,76-79] (for review: [80]), and therefore the present study does not exclude that CPK3 and CPK6 have additional functions in other tissues. The present study demonstrates important functions of the CPK3 and CPK6 CDPKs in control of stomatal movements and in ABA and Ca2+ regulation of guard cell S-type anion channels and unexpectedly also in ABA regulation of Ca2+-permeable ICa channels.
###end p 35
###begin p 36
###xml 35 37 35 37 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 125 127 125 127 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b081">81</xref>
###xml 132 134 132 134 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 258 260 258 260 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 269 281 269 281 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CBL1/SCaBP5,</italic>
###xml 341 343 341 343 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 385 387 385 387 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b026">26</xref>
###xml 399 401 399 401 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b082">82</xref>
###xml 435 438 435 438 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CBL</italic>
###xml 440 444 440 444 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CBL9</italic>
###xml 569 580 569 580 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis</italic>
###xml 648 650 648 650 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b027">27</xref>
###xml 709 713 709 713 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CDPK</italic>
Although many studies have shown Ca2+-dependent steps in guard cell signal transduction and in plant ion channel regulation [81], Ca2+ sensor-encoding genes that function as positive transducers in these responses have remained unknown. A calcineurin-like Ca2+ sensor, CBL1/SCaBP5, has been reported to function as a negatively regulating Ca2+ sensor in ABA signaling in guard cells ([26], but see [82]). Knock-out mutation of another CBL, CBL9, resulted in ABA hypersensitive phenotypes in seed germination, root and shoot growth, and ABA-inducible gene expression in Arabidopsis, indicating its function as a negative regulator of ABA signaling [27]. In the present study, guard cell expression analyses of CDPK genes aided in narrowing the number of candidate genes that may function in this system. Furthermore, the guard cell system has also allowed us to pursue detailed mechanistic and cellular analyses revealing functions of specific CDPKs in planta.
###end p 36
###begin title 37
###xml 20 22 20 22 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
CDPKs Function in Ca2+-Reactive Stomatal Closure and S-Type Anion Channel Activation
###end title 37
###begin p 38
###xml 3 5 3 5 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 6 9 6 9 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt</sub>
###xml 53 55 53 55 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 131 133 131 133 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 153 155 153 155 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b029">29</xref>
###xml 186 188 186 188 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 244 246 244 246 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 269 271 269 271 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b029">29</xref>
###xml 272 274 272 274 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b031">31</xref>
###xml 279 281 279 281 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 350 352 350 352 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 368 376 368 376 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 401 403 401 403 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 479 487 479 487 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g007">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 513 515 513 515 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 563 571 563 571 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 645 647 645 647 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 706 708 706 708 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 747 749 747 749 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b029">29</xref>
###xml 783 791 783 791 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 827 829 827 829 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 886 894 886 894 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g007">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 975 977 975 977 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 993 995 993 995 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1039 1043 1039 1043 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CDPK</italic>
###xml 1148 1150 1148 1150 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b054">54</xref>
###xml 1220 1222 1220 1222 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
[Ca2+]cyt elevation in guard cells causes a rapid "Ca2+-reactive" stomatal closure response, irrespective of the above threshold Ca2+ elevation pattern [29]. In contrast, a long-term "Ca2+-programmed" stomatal closure is modulated by imposed Ca2+ transient parameters [29-31]. Ca2+-dependent stomatal movements were analyzed in response to imposed Ca2+ transients. In cpk3cpk6 double mutant plants, Ca2+-reactive stomatal closure was significantly reduced compared to wild-type (Figure 7). However, the partial Ca2+ transient-induced stomatal closing response of cpk3cpk6 double mutant plants was maintained in white light more than 2 h after Ca2+ transients were terminated. Thus, the imposed long-term Ca2+-programmed stomatal closure response [29] appears to be functional in the cpk3cpk6 double mutant, whereas the rapid Ca2+-reactive stomatal closure response is clearly impaired (Figure 7). The presented data provide genetic evidence for a mechanistic separation of Ca2+-reactive and Ca2+-programmed stomatal closure. Several other CDPK transcripts are expressed in guard cells as determined by oligonucleotide-based microarray experiments [54]. It is possible that other guard cell-expressed CDPKs function in Ca2+-programmed stomatal closure.
###end p 38
###begin p 39
###xml 82 84 82 84 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 122 124 122 124 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b016">16</xref>
###xml 125 127 125 127 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b032">32</xref>
###xml 165 167 165 167 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 400 402 400 402 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b016">16</xref>
###xml 424 426 424 426 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 478 482 478 482 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3</italic>
###xml 487 491 487 491 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6</italic>
###xml 606 608 606 608 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 609 612 609 612 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt</sub>
###xml 669 677 669 677 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g009">Figure 9</xref>
###xml 684 690 684 690 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 695 701 695 701 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 943 947 943 947 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK6</italic>
###xml 988 994 988 994 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 1048 1054 1048 1054 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 1275 1277 1275 1277 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b083">83</xref>
###xml 1344 1350 1344 1350 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 1841 1843 1841 1843 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1905 1907 1905 1907 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1944 1953 1944 1953 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g002">Figures 2</xref>
###xml 1955 1956 1955 1956 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g007">7</xref>
###xml 1962 1963 1962 1963 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g009">9</xref>
###xml 1966 1968 1966 1968 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b029">29</xref>
Previous studies have provided evidence that phosphorylation events function in Ca2+ activation of S-type anion channels [16,32] (see Introduction). The cytosolic Ca2+ activation of S-type anion channels requires the presence of hydrolyzable ATP in the patch-clamp electrode, and this channel activation is abolished by the general serine/threonine protein kinase inhibitors K252a and staurosporine [16]. The finding that Ca2+ activation of S-type anion channels is impaired in cpk3 and cpk6 gene disruption mutants provides molecular genetic evidence for this model and suggests that CDPKs function in [Ca2+]cyt perception upstream of S-type anion channel activation (Figure 9). The cpk6-1 and cpk6-2 alleles exhibit similar defects in all of the phenotypes that were examined, suggesting that both alleles are strong alleles. Although both alleles show no expression of full-length cDNA, a faint band representing residual transcript of the CPK6 open reading frame was amplified in the cpk6-2 allele (8% or less of wild-type level). However, the cpk6-2 transcript is lacking the wild-type origin of transcription. Furthermore, this transcript also lacks the first exon of the wild-type cDNA, and 5' UTRs have been shown to play roles in enhancing translational efficiency [83]. Together, these data indicate that the greatly reduced level of cpk6-2 transcripts and the absence of the first exon are sufficient to cause the strong phenotypes observed in this study. Future direct investigation of the model that CDPKs phosphorylate important targets during S-type anion channel activation will require identification of the molecular components that encode these ion channels or upstream regulators. CPK3 and CPK6 may have distinct functions in the upstream ion channel regulation pathways. The present findings point to a model in which Ca2+ activation of S-type anion channels functions in the rapid Ca2+-reactive stomatal closure response (Figures 2, 7, and 9) [29].
###end p 39
###begin title 40
###xml 36 38 36 38 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
CDPKs, R-Type Anion Channels, and Ca2+-Independent Signaling
###end title 40
###begin p 41
###xml 4 6 4 6 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 133 135 133 135 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 180 182 180 182 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b013">13</xref>
###xml 183 185 183 185 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b016">16</xref>
###xml 186 188 186 188 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b025">25</xref>
###xml 189 191 189 191 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b028">28</xref>
###xml 192 194 192 194 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b084">84</xref>
###xml 195 197 195 197 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b086">86</xref>
###xml 214 215 214 215 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b002">2</xref>
###xml 216 217 216 217 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b004">4</xref>
###xml 218 220 218 220 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b087">87</xref>
###xml 226 228 226 228 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 355 373 355 373 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Commelina communis</named-content>
###xml 375 377 375 377 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b025">25</xref>
###xml 450 452 450 452 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 486 488 486 488 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b086">86</xref>
###xml 489 491 489 491 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b088">88</xref>
###xml 512 514 512 514 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 589 591 589 591 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 682 684 682 684 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 713 724 713 724 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis</italic>
###xml 759 768 759 768 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g003">Figures 3</xref>
###xml 770 771 770 771 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g004">4</xref>
###xml 843 845 843 845 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 355 373 <span type="species:ncbi:4744">Commelina communis</span>
A Ca2+-independent ABA signal transduction branch has been implicated in guard cells, based on data in which ABA-induced cytosolic Ca2+ increases were not observed in guard cells [13,16,25,28,84-86] (for reviews: [2-4,87]). Ca2+-dependent or -independent ABA signaling pathways have been reported to be emphasized depending on physiological conditions in Commelina communis [25]. The abolishment of ABA-induced stomatal closing by injection of the Ca2+ chelator BAPTA into guard cells [86,88] indicates that a Ca2+-independent branch within the ABA signaling network would interact with Ca2+-dependent mechanisms. The present study provides direct molecular genetic evidence that Ca2+ sensors function within the Arabidopsis guard cell ABA signaling network (Figures 3, 4, and 6A) and provides a genetic basis to analyze interactions with a Ca2+-independent pathway.
###end p 41
###begin p 42
###xml 85 87 85 87 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b062">62</xref>
###xml 88 90 88 90 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b070">70</xref>
###xml 91 93 91 93 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b073">73</xref>
###xml 94 96 94 96 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b089">89</xref>
###xml 227 237 227 237 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Vicia faba</named-content>
###xml 251 253 251 253 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b062">62</xref>
###xml 254 256 254 256 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b073">73</xref>
###xml 278 280 278 280 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 369 376 369 376 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">V. faba</named-content>
###xml 416 418 416 418 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 451 452 451 452 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 465 467 465 467 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b071">71</xref>
###xml 473 481 473 481 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 594 602 594 602 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g008">Figure 8</xref>
###xml 656 664 656 664 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g006">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 667 674 667 674 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="pbio-0040327-t001">Table 1</xref>
###xml 774 782 774 782 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g009">Figure 9</xref>
###xml 882 893 882 893 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis</italic>
###xml 895 903 895 903 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g008">Figure 8</xref>
###xml 909 916 909 916 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">V. faba</named-content>
###xml 918 920 918 920 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b086">86</xref>
###xml 948 950 948 950 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 951 954 951 954 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt</sub>
###xml 996 998 996 998 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1021 1028 1021 1028 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">V. faba</named-content>
###xml 1121 1122 1121 1122 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1177 1179 1177 1179 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1196 1198 1196 1198 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b016">16</xref>
###xml 1199 1201 1199 1201 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b067">67</xref>
###xml 1202 1204 1202 1204 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b069">69</xref>
###xml 1223 1225 1223 1225 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1271 1279 1271 1279 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g009">Figure 9</xref>
###xml 1331 1339 1331 1339 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 1466 1475 1466 1475 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g002">Figures 2</xref>
###xml 1477 1478 1477 1478 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g003">3</xref>
###xml 1553 1555 1553 1555 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b089">89</xref>
###xml 1558 1566 1558 1566 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g009">Figure 9</xref>
###xml 227 237 <span type="species:ncbi:3906">Vicia faba</span>
###xml 369 376 <span type="species:ncbi:3906">V. faba</span>
###xml 909 916 <span type="species:ncbi:3906">V. faba</span>
###xml 1021 1028 <span type="species:ncbi:3906">V. faba</span>
Several studies have indicated a role for R-type anion channels in stomatal closure [62,70-73,89], in addition to S-type anion channels. ABA activation of R-type anion channels was recently directly demonstrated in a subset of Vicia faba guard cells [62,73]. Direct cytosolic Ca2+ activation of R-type channels has not yet been shown, although R-type anion channels in V. faba guard cells have been proposed to be Ca2+ activated based on external CaCl2 activation [71]. In cpk3cpk6 double mutant guard cells, R-type anion channel activity was not greatly impaired under the imposed conditions (Figure 8). The partial closure of stomata in response to ABA (Figure 6A, Table 1) may thus be explained by overlapping physiological functions of R-type and S-type anion channels (Figure 9). In the present study and in a recent study, R-type anion currents were recorded in patch-clamped Arabidopsis (Figure 8) and V. faba [86] guard cells at resting [Ca2+]cyt and were proposed to be activated in a Ca2+-independent manner in V. faba. However, in both studies, guard cells were preincubated in a solution containing 40 mM CaCl2 or more prior to patch clamping which would elevate Ca2+ in guard cells [16,67,69], and therefore Ca2+-independent R-type anion channel activation (Figure 9) will require further investigation. The presented cpk3cpk6 mutant data provide first genetic evidence that parallel pathways function in regulation of R-type and S-type anion channels (Figures 2, 3, and 8), even though these anion channels may share molecular components [89] (Figure 9).
###end p 42
###begin p 43
###xml 75 83 75 83 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 111 120 111 120 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g002">Figures 2</xref>
###xml 123 124 123 124 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g002">2</xref>
###xml 127 128 127 128 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g003">3</xref>
###xml 134 135 134 135 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g003">3</xref>
###xml 190 192 190 192 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 249 260 249 260 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis</italic>
###xml 341 349 341 349 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 431 442 431 442 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis</italic>
###xml 546 547 545 546 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 651 652 650 651 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 760 762 759 761 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b073">73</xref>
###xml 767 768 766 767 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 802 810 801 809 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 899 907 898 906 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 955 956 954 955 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1198 1207 1197 1206 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3 cpk6</italic>
###xml 1484 1486 1483 1485 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b090">90</xref>
Residual small S-type anion channel currents were consistently observed in cpk3cpk6 double mutant guard cells (Figures 2B, 2C, 3C and 3D), which should also contribute to partial ABA- and Ca2+-induced stomatal closing. The rate of anion efflux from Arabidopsis guard cells can be estimated, to predict whether the residual anion currents in cpk3cpk6 double mutants can close stomata within a physiological response. Cell volume of Arabidopsis GCPs was estimated at 0.11 pL according to the average diameter of protoplasts (6 mum). An estimated Cl- concentration decrease from 400 mM to 100 mM during ABA-induced stomatal closure would correspond to Cl- efflux of 33.9 fmol/cell. The membrane potential of guard cells treated with ABA was approximately -50 mV [73]. Cl- efflux currents in wild-type and cpk3cpk6 double mutant guard cells at -50 mV were approximately -60 pA and -25 pA, respectively (Figure 3E). These S-type anion currents correspond to Cl- efflux rates of 37.3 fmol/min for wild-type and 15.54 fmol/min for the double mutant. This estimate shows that during the slow onset of drought that occurs over several days in intact plants, the residual S-type and R-type anion currents in cpk3 cpk6 double mutants should be sufficient for a physiological stomatal closing response. Similarly, previous estimates have predicted that ion channel activities are over 10-fold higher in biological membranes than required for a typical response, due to their high transport rate [90]. This estimate also highlights the power of analyzing individual ion channel targets for characterizing CDPK functions in plants.
###end p 43
###begin p 44
###xml 123 125 123 125 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 158 161 158 161 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk</italic>
###xml 171 180 171 180 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g006">Figures 6</xref>
###xml 186 187 186 187 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g007">7</xref>
###xml 211 213 211 213 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 374 382 374 382 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 403 412 403 412 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g002">Figures 2</xref>
###xml 414 415 414 415 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g003">3</xref>
###xml 421 422 421 422 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g008">8</xref>
###xml 462 464 462 464 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 512 521 512 521 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g006">Figures 6</xref>
###xml 523 524 523 524 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g007">7</xref>
