###xml 530 531 530 531 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g009">9</xref>
###xml 583 585 583 585 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 619 621 619 621 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b091">91</xref>
###xml 622 624 622 624 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b092">92</xref>
It is possible that additional CDPKs contribute to activation of the residual S-type anion current activity. The partial Ca2+-induced stomatal closure in the cpk mutants (Figures 6B and 7) can be explained by Ca2+ activation of residual S-type anion channel currents. In summary, the lack of R-type anion channel activity alteration and the residual S-type anion current in cpk3cpk6 mutant guard cells (Figures 2, 3, and 8) correlate with the partial ABA- and Ca2+-induced stomatal closing responses found here (Figures 6, 7, and 9) and may also reflect a contribution of parallel Ca2+-independent and/or pH-dependent [91,92] signaling mechanisms.
###end p 44
###begin title 45
###xml 40 42 40 42 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
CDPK Mutants Impair ABA Activation of Ca2+-Permeable Channels
###end title 45
###begin p 46
###xml 33 35 33 35 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 69 77 69 77 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 105 113 105 113 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 291 293 291 293 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b053">53</xref>
###xml 465 467 461 463 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 486 494 482 490 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g009">Figure 9</xref>
###xml 497 499 493 495 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b065">65</xref>
###xml 593 595 589 591 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 616 624 612 620 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g009">Figure 9</xref>
###xml 627 629 623 625 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b015">15</xref>
###xml 630 632 626 628 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b017">17</xref>
###xml 633 635 629 631 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b018">18</xref>
###xml 636 638 632 634 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b081">81</xref>
Unexpectedly, ABA activation of ICa channel currents was impaired in cpk3cpk6 double mutant guard cells (Figure 4). Impairment in ROS signaling partially impairs rather than abolishes ABA-induced stomatal movement responses, consistent with their activity mainly at hyperpolarized voltages [53]. The present findings are consistent with a model in which additional signaling branches function in the ABA signal transduction network parallel to the ABA --> ROS --> ICa signaling branch (Figure 9) [65]. Several parallel pathways function in the ABA signaling network, including intracellular Ca2+-release mechanisms (Figure 9) [15,17,18,81].
###end p 46
###begin p 47
###xml 61 63 61 63 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 301 309 301 309 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 315 316 315 316 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g004">4</xref>
###xml 370 372 370 372 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b045">45</xref>
###xml 373 375 373 375 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b093">93</xref>
###xml 376 378 376 378 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b095">95</xref>
###xml 396 398 396 398 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 451 453 451 453 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b016">16</xref>
###xml 454 456 454 456 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b032">32</xref>
###xml 526 534 526 534 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 580 582 580 582 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 608 616 608 616 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g004">Figure 4</xref>
Interestingly, in wild-type guard cells, ABA could activate ICa channels even when cells were preexposed to the general serine/threonine kinase inhibitor K252a and the cytosol of guard cells was dialyzed with an ATP-free solution for longer than 15 min in whole-cell recordings prior to ABA exposure (Figure 4J and 4K). K252a inhibits CDPK activities in diverse plants [45,93-95] and abolishes Ca2+ activation of S-type anion channels in guard cells [16,32]. These data indicate the following possible mechanisms by which the cpk3cpk6 mutant alleles may impair ABA activation of ICa channels in guard cells (Figure 4):
###end p 47
###begin p 48
###xml 122 124 116 118 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 151 159 145 153 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g009">Figure 9</xref>
###xml 209 211 203 205 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 268 270 262 264 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 281 283 275 277 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b096">96</xref>
###xml 328 336 322 330 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g009">Figure 9</xref>
###xml 426 428 420 422 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 439 447 433 441 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g009">Figure 9</xref>
1. CPK3 and CPK6 may not be directly activated in response to exogenous ABA within the ABA --> NADPH oxidase --> ROS --> ICa channel signaling branch (Figure 9). But these CDPKs are necessary for maintaining ICa channel activation in a parallel regulation pathway of ICa channels [96] that also regulates S-type anion channels (Figure 9B). In this model, ABA regulation of S-type anion channels is not strictly downstream of ICa channels (Figure 9B).
###end p 48
###begin p 49
###xml 23 25 23 25 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 75 77 75 77 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 99 101 99 101 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 112 120 112 120 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g009">Figure 9</xref>
2. CDPKs may regulate ICa channels in a feedback loop by which cytosolic Ca2+ elevations regulate ICa channels (Figure 9A).
###end p 49
###begin p 50
###xml 79 87 79 87 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 162 164 162 164 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 226 232 226 232 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">abi1&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 237 243 237 243 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">abi2&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 582 584 582 584 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b066">66</xref>
###xml 607 615 607 615 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 714 716 714 716 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 753 764 753 764 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis</italic>
###xml 850 858 850 858 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 864 865 864 865 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g004">4</xref>
3. The present findings can also be explained by an alternative model in which cpk3cpk6 mutation affects gene expression in such a manner that ABA activation of ICa channels is impaired. Similarly, the effects of the dominant abi1-1 and abi2-1 protein phosphatase 2C (PP2C) mutants on ABA responses could in principle result from indirect effects of these mutations on these ABA signal components, because these are dominant mutations and no pharmacological PP2C inhibitors are available to test effects of short-term PP2C impairment on channel regulation, as previously discussed [66]. This model in which cpk3cpk6 may affect transcriptional or translational responses would be consistent with the activation of ICa currents in patch-clamped wild-type Arabidopsis guard cells without added cytoplasmic ATP and in the simultaneous presence of K252a (Figure 4J and 4K).
###end p 50
###begin p 51
###xml 15 22 15 22 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">V. faba</named-content>
###xml 75 86 75 86 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis</italic>
###xml 141 143 141 143 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 166 174 166 174 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 191 198 191 198 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">V. faba</named-content>
###xml 246 248 246 248 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 336 338 336 338 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 424 426 424 426 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 461 468 461 468 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">V. faba</named-content>
###xml 470 472 470 472 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b096">96</xref>
###xml 475 483 475 483 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g009">Figure 9</xref>
###xml 510 521 510 521 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis</italic>
###xml 664 666 658 660 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 694 703 688 697 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g004">Figures 4</xref>
###xml 708 709 702 703 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g009">9</xref>
###xml 751 762 745 756 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis</italic>
###xml 767 772 761 766 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Vicia</italic>
###xml 913 915 907 909 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b032">32</xref>
###xml 916 918 910 912 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b055">55</xref>
###xml 919 921 913 915 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b059">59</xref>
###xml 922 924 916 918 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b086">86</xref>
###xml 925 927 919 921 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b097">97</xref>
###xml 928 930 922 924 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b098">98</xref>
###xml 15 22 <span type="species:ncbi:3906">V. faba</span>
###xml 191 198 <span type="species:ncbi:3906">V. faba</span>
###xml 461 468 <span type="species:ncbi:3906">V. faba</span>
Experiments in V. faba guard cells show different responses than wild-type Arabidopsis guard cells that may shed light on the impairment in ICa channel activation in cpk3cpk6 guard cells. In V. faba guard cells, K252a inhibits ABA activation of ICa currents and the protein phosphatase inhibitors calyculin A and okadaic acid activate ICa channel currents, suggesting that phosphorylation/dephosphorylation events regulate ICa channels in a parallel pathway in V. faba [96] (Figure 9). The present findings in Arabidopsis guard cells would predict a requirement for CDPK-dependent phosphorylation, prior to ABA activation of the ABA --> NADPH oxidase --> ROS --> ICa channel regulation branch (Figures 4 and 9B). Previous analyses have indicated that Arabidopsis and Vicia guard cells emphasize different components of the guard cell signaling network, including differential phosphorylation-dependent responses [32,55,59,86,97,98]. In this respect, further comparative analyses among species should be useful in illuminating new signaling network mechanisms and branches.
###end p 51
###begin p 52
###xml 171 173 171 173 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 234 236 234 236 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 248 250 248 250 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
Further studies will be necessary to distinguish the above models. The present study, however, provides a first characterization of a genetic mutation that impairs both Ca2+ activation of S-type anion channels and ABA activation of Ca2+-permeable ICa channels, indicating closer interactions among mechanisms that regulate these two classes of ion channels in guard cells than previously modeled.
###end p 52
###begin title 53
Conclusions
###end title 53
###begin p 54
###xml 78 80 78 80 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 182 186 182 186 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK6</italic>
###xml 191 195 191 195 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK3</italic>
###xml 362 366 362 366 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CDPK</italic>
###xml 374 378 374 378 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK3</italic>
###xml 383 387 383 387 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK6</italic>
###xml 395 400 395 400 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CDPKs</italic>
###xml 423 425 423 425 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 489 491 489 491 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 503 505 503 505 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 592 600 592 600 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
###xml 668 670 668 670 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 717 719 717 719 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 857 865 857 865 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3cpk6</italic>
In summary, in this study, we provide direct molecular genetic evidence for Ca2+ sensors that function as positive transducers in stomatal ABA signaling and demonstrate functions of CPK6 and CPK3 in plant ion channel regulation in defined guard cell signal transduction elements. We functionally characterize disruption mutations in the two guard cell-expressed CDPK genes, CPK3 and CPK6. These CDPKs function in ABA and Ca2+ activation of S-type anion channels and in ABA regulation of Ca2+-permeable ICa cation channels but not in R-type anion channel activity in guard cells. Furthermore, cpk3cpk6 double mutants partially impair ABA-induced stomatal closure and Ca2+-reactive stomatal closure but not long-term Ca2+-programmed stomatal closure. Partial stomatal closing responses and differential regulation of R- and S-type anion current activities in cpk3cpk6 mutant guard cells are consistent with models proposing parallel signaling mechanisms in a branched guard cell signal transduction network. Future cell-type-specific analyses of CDPKs may illuminate further cellular functions of this protein kinase family in plants.
###end p 54
###begin title 55
Materials and Methods
###end title 55
###begin title 56
Plant growth.
###end title 56
###begin p 57
###xml 0 20 0 20 <named-content xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" content-type="genus-species">Arabidopsis thaliana</named-content>
###xml 232 234 231 233 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;2</sup>
###xml 236 238 235 237 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;1</sup>
###xml 0 20 <span type="species:ncbi:3702">Arabidopsis thaliana</span>
Arabidopsis thaliana plants (Columbia ecotype) were grown in soil (Sungro Special blend Professional Growing Mix; Seba Beach, Alberta, Canada) in a growth room under a 16-h-light/8-h-dark cycle at a photon fluence rate of 75 mumol m-2 s-1 and a temperature of 20 degreesC.
###end p 57
###begin title 58
Identification of CDPK genes expressed in guard cells.
###end title 58
###begin p 59
###xml 127 129 127 129 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b055">55</xref>
###xml 538 540 538 540 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b055">55</xref>
###xml 775 777 775 777 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b055">55</xref>
###xml 980 984 980 984 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3</italic>
###xml 989 993 989 993 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6</italic>
###xml 1128 1130 1128 1130 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b053">53</xref>
###xml 1131 1133 1131 1133 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b055">55</xref>
Degenerate oligomer-based RT-PCR was used to identify guard cell-expressed CDPK genes from guard cell-enriched cDNA libraries [55]. Degenerate oligomers were designed from two highly conserved regions that were selected from aligned CDPK peptide sequences: HRDLKPENF and DG(K/R)I(D/N)(Y/F)(E/S)EF. The degenerate oligomers used to amplify guard cell-expressed CDPK genes are as follows: 5'-caymgigayytiaarccigaraaytt-3' and 5'-aaytcitciwaityiatiykiccrtc-3'. Total RNA was extracted from guard cell-enriched epidermal strips as described [55] with the TriZOL reagent (Invitrogen, Carlsbad, California, United States). cDNA was synthesized using the First-Strand cDNA Synthesis Kit (Amersham-Pharmacia Biotech, Little Chalfont, United Kingdom). PCR was performed as described [55]. PCR products were cloned into the pGEM-T Easy vector (Promega, Madison, Wisconsin, United States). The sequences of the cloned PCR products were determined by regular sequencing reactions. Homozygous cpk3 and cpk6 single and double mutants were identified using gene-specific primers and primers that match T-DNA sequences as described previously [53,55].
###end p 59
###begin title 60
Cell-type-specific expression analyses and RT-PCR.
###end title 60
###begin p 61
###xml 87 98 87 98 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis</italic>
###xml 123 125 123 125 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b054">54</xref>
###xml 321 329 321 329 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 349 353 349 353 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">KAT1</italic>
###xml 376 379 376 379 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CBP</italic>
###xml 406 412 406 412 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ACTIN2</italic>
GCPs and mesophyll cell protoplasts were isolated by enzymatic digestion from 4-wk-old Arabidopsis plants as described in [54]. Total RNA was extracted from GCPs and mesophyll cell protoplasts with TriZOL reagent. Gene-specific primers for CPK3 and CPK6 were localized downstream of the DNA insertion sites as indicated (Figure 1B). For analyses of KAT1 (AGI No.: At5g46240), CBP (AGI No.: At4g33050), and ACTIN2 (AGI No.: At3g18780) mRNAs, gene-specific primers were used for amplifications.
###end p 61
###begin title 62
Patch-clamp analyses.
###end title 62
###begin p 63
###xml 25 27 25 27 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 48 59 48 59 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis</italic>
###xml 140 141 140 141 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b009">9</xref>
###xml 156 158 156 158 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 161 163 161 163 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b065">65</xref>
S- and R-type anion and ICa channel currents in Arabidopsis guard cells were recorded as published previously and described below (S-type: [9], R-type and ICa: [65]). Patch-clamp data were recorded using an Axopatch 200 amplifier and pClamp software and analyzed with Axograph software (Axon Instruments, Union City, California, United States).
###end p 63
###begin p 64
###xml 98 99 98 99 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 161 162 161 162 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 189 191 188 190 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 242 243 241 242 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 254 255 253 254 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 368 369 367 368 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 401 409 400 408 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g002">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 437 438 436 437 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b009">9</xref>
###xml 550 552 549 551 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 554 562 553 561 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g003">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 608 609 607 608 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 631 633 630 632 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 681 692 680 691 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis</italic>
###xml 699 700 698 699 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b009">9</xref>
###xml 759 761 758 760 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 839 841 838 840 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 876 878 875 877 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b055">55</xref>
###xml 958 960 957 959 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;1</sup>
###xml 1130 1131 1129 1130 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b005">5</xref>
###xml 1445 1448 1444 1447 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk</italic>
To measure whole-cell S-type anion currents, the pipette solution contained 150 mM CsCl, 2 mM MgCl2, 6.7 mM EGTA, 5 mM MgATP, 10 mM HEPES-Tris (pH 7.1), and CaCl2 to result in 2 muM free Ca2+. The bath solution contained 30 mM CsCl, 2 mM MgCl2, 1 mM CaCl2, and 10 mM MES-Tris (pH 5.6). Guard cells were extracellularly preincubated in the same solution with 40 mM CaCl2 added prior to patch-clamping (Figure 2), as previously described [9]; except for in ABA regulation analyses in which guard cells were preincubated in a solution containing 1 mM Ca2+ (Figure 3). Pretreatment of protoplasts with 40 mM CaCl2 allows analyses of Ca2+ activation of S-type anion channel currents in Arabidopsis (see [9] for details), and pretreatment with 1 mM extracellular Ca2+ allows analyses of ABA regulation of S-type anion channels while cytosolic Ca2+ is elevated, as previously shown [55]. Osmolarity of the solutions was adjusted with sorbitol to 500 and 485 mmol kg-1, respectively. The liquid junction potential was 0.5 mV. The membrane voltage was stepped from the holding potential of +35 mV to -145 mV for 40 s in -30-mV decrements [5]. The interpulse period was 12 s. No leak subtraction was performed. Recordings were made 7 to 10 min after access to the whole-cell configuration. For ABA activation of S-type channels, ABA was added to the bath solution prior to patch-clamping and seal formation. To test the robustness of ABA insensitivity in cpk mutant guard cells, 50 muM ABA was applied to guard cells.
###end p 64
###begin p 65
###xml 12 14 12 14 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 74 75 74 75 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 174 175 174 175 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 265 266 265 266 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 366 368 366 368 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;1</sup>
###xml 460 462 460 462 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 584 586 584 586 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 784 786 784 786 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;1</sup>
###xml 934 935 934 935 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 936 937 936 937 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 960 962 960 962 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
To measure ICa channel currents, the pipette solution contained 10 mM BaCl2, 0.1 mM DTT, 4 mM EGTA, and 10 mM HEPES-Tris (pH 7.1), and the bath solution contained 100 mM BaCl2, 0.1 mM DTT, and 10 mM MES-Tris (pH 5.6). Guard cells were not preincubated in 40 mM CaCl2 in these experiments. Osmolarity of the solutions was adjusted with sorbitol to 500 and 485 mmol kg-1, respectively. NADPH (5 mM) was added to the pipette for the measurement of ABA-activated ICa currents. ABA was added extracellularly 16 min after whole-cell recordings began. In typical experiments, activation of ICa was observed within 1 min of ABA addition and continued for longer than 30 min. The voltage was ramped from -18 to -198 mV (after liquid junction potential correction) with a ramp speed of 180 mV s-1. In a standard measurement, the ramp protocol was applied 16 times to obtain an average current for a cell. The interpulse period was 1 min. When H2O2 (5 mM) activation of ICa was measured, the same procedures, analysis of average currents, and timing of application were used as for ABA regulation experiments.
###end p 65
###begin p 66
###xml 80 81 80 81 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 83 84 83 84 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">4</sub>
###xml 86 88 86 88 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b099">99</xref>
###xml 100 101 100 101 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 125 126 125 126 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 204 206 204 206 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;1</sup>
###xml 246 247 246 247 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 258 259 258 259 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 336 338 336 338 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;1</sup>
###xml 452 454 452 454 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;1</sup>
###xml 553 554 553 554 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">t</italic>
To measure R-type anion channel currents, the pipette solution contained 75 mM K2SO4 [99], 2 mM MgCl2, 5 mM EGTA, 2.5 mM CaCl2, and 10 mM HEPES-Tris (pH 7.2) and the osmolarity was adjusted to 500 mmol kg-1. The bath solution contained 50 mM CaCl2, 2 mM MgCl2, and 10 mM MES-Tris (pH 5.6), and the osmolarity was adjusted to 485 mmol kg-1 with sorbitol. The voltage was ramped from the holding potential of 0 mV to -200 mV with a ramp speed of -20 mV s-1. Significance of differences between data sets was assessed by noncoupled double-tailed Student's t-test analysis.
###end p 66
###begin title 67
Stomatal movement analyses.
###end title 67
###begin p 68
###xml 86 97 86 97 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis</italic>
###xml 166 167 165 166 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 270 272 262 264 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;2</sup>
###xml 274 276 266 268 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;1</sup>
###xml 363 364 355 356 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 404 406 396 398 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 475 476 467 468 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 551 564 543 556 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-2cpk6&#8211;2,</italic>
###xml 589 597 581 589 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g006">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 620 622 612 614 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 648 650 640 642 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 689 701 681 693 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-2cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 830 842 822 834 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-2cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 909 910 901 902 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 931 932 922 923 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 934 935 925 926 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 957 958 947 948 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 960 961 950 951 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">p</italic>
###xml 984 985 973 974 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1005 1017 994 1006 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-2cpk6&#8211;2</italic>
###xml 1519 1522 1507 1510 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b100">100</xref>
###xml 1523 1526 1511 1514 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b101">101</xref>
###xml 1585 1593 1573 1581 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g006">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 1730 1739 1718 1727 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3 cpk6</italic>
To measure changes in stomatal aperture, excised rosette leaves from 3- to 4.5-wk-old Arabidopsis plants were floated on 3 ml of opening buffer (5 mM KCl, 50 muM CaCl2, and 10 mM MES-Tris [pH 5.6]) for 2.5 h at 20 degreesC under light (photon fluency rate of 125 mumol m-2 s-1), so that the opening solution was taken up through petioles. After 2.5 h, ABA or CaCl2 was added to the opening buffer. For Ca2+-induced stomatal closing assays, opening solution without added CaCl2 was used. Leaves were incubated for an additional 3 h, and in the case of cpk3-2cpk6-2, for 3 h and for 45 min (Figure 6), after addition of Ca2+. Similar impairment in Ca2+-induced stomatal closure was found in cpk3-2cpk6-2 double mutant plants compared to wild-type after both 45 min. and 3 h. Furthermore, similar stomatal responses were observed in cpk3-2cpk6-2 plants 45 min. and 3 h after stimulation in parallel experiments (p > 0.50 at 0 muM CaCl2, p > 0.50 at 10 muM CaCl2, p > 0.45 at 100 muM CaCl2 (45 min versus 3 h cpk3-2cpk6-2 data). Leaves were blended in opening solution in a Waring commercial blender (Waring Commercial, Torrington, Connecticut, United States) for 30 s. The blended material was filtered on a 100-mum nylon mesh, and epidermal strips were placed onto a microscope slide with a glass coverslip. The ratio of stomatal width to length was measured with an inverted microscope. Width was measured as the distance between the inner walls of the stomata, and length was measured as the length of the guard cells [100,101]. Data from stomatal ratios mirrored stomatal width data (Figure 6). For each sample, 20 to 30 stomata were measured. Blind experiments were also conducted, in which the genotype of leaves (wild-type or cpk3 cpk6 mutant and the added stimuli) was unknown to the experimenter.
###end p 68
###begin title 69
###xml 10 12 10 12 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
Imposed Ca2+ oscillation responses.
###end title 69
###begin p 70
###xml 21 23 21 23 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 731 733 729 731 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;2</sup>
###xml 735 737 733 735 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;1</sup>
###xml 759 761 757 759 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 762 765 760 763 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt</sub>
###xml 905 906 903 904 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 967 969 965 967 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 970 973 968 971 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt</sub>
###xml 1026 1028 1024 1026 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1029 1032 1027 1030 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt</sub>
###xml 1041 1043 1039 1041 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b068">68</xref>
To measure imposed Ca2+ oscillation-induced stomatal closure, epidermal peels were prepared by using Hollister medical adhesive (Stock No. 7730; Hollister Inc., Libertyville, Illinois, United States) to attach a leaf abaxial side down onto a coverslip. A razor blade was used to carefully remove the cuticle and mesophyll layers of the leaf, leaving the lower leaf epidermal layer containing stomatal complexes intact. The coverslip was then sealed with grease to the bottom of a custom microscope slide with a 2-cm-diameter hole cut in the center, creating a 200-mul well. The well was then filled with depolarizing buffer (50 mM KCl and 10 mM MES-Tris [pH 5.6]), and the leaf segment was incubated for 2.5 h in light (125 mumol m-2 s-1) to open stomata. [Ca2+]cyt transients were imposed by rapid exchange of the chamber buffer between depolarizing buffer and hyperpolarizing buffer (1 mM KCl, 1 mM CaCl2, 10 mM MES-Tris [pH 5.6]). Depolarizing buffer decreases [Ca2+]cyt levels, whereas hyperpolarizing buffer increases [Ca2+]cyt levels [68]. For each experiment, four separate transients with an approximately 10-min period were imposed. Stomatal apertures of several individually mapped stomata were measured at the indicated time points for 3 h after the start of imposed oscillations.
###end p 70
###begin p 71
###xml 12 14 12 14 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 55 57 55 57 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 58 61 58 61 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt</sub>
###xml 172 175 172 175 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b102">102</xref>
###xml 188 200 188 200 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3-1cpk6&#8211;1</italic>
###xml 286 288 286 288 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 350 352 350 352 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 550 552 548 550 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 559 560 557 558 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 630 631 628 629 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 652 653 650 651 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 728 731 726 729 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b103">103</xref>
###xml 926 927 924 925 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 933 934 931 932 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 941 944 939 942 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b104">104</xref>
###xml 945 948 943 946 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b105">105</xref>
###xml 1098 1099 1096 1097 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1105 1106 1103 1104 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 1181 1183 1179 1181 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1184 1187 1182 1185 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt</sub>
###xml 1197 1200 1195 1198 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b102">102</xref>
###xml 1347 1348 1345 1346 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1419 1421 1417 1419 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1486 1488 1484 1486 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b029">29</xref>
###xml 1532 1534 1530 1532 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1589 1591 1587 1589 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1637 1639 1635 1637 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1748 1749 1746 1747 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1759 1760 1757 1758 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 1813 1816 1811 1814 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b106">106</xref>
###xml 1901 1903 1899 1901 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 1935 1936 1933 1934 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 2000 2009 1998 2007 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g010">Figure 10</xref>
###xml 2103 2104 2101 2102 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 2133 2135 2131 2133 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 2156 2157 2154 2155 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 2185 2187 2183 2185 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 2285 2286 2283 2284 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 2317 2319 2315 2317 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 2348 2357 2346 2355 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="pbio-0040327-g010">Figure 10</xref>
###xml 2391 2393 2389 2391 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b029">29</xref>
###xml 2394 2397 2392 2395 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b104">104</xref>
###xml 2398 2401 2396 2399 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b105">105</xref>
Cytosolic Ca2+ concentration changes during imposed [Ca2+]cyt transient experiments were confirmed by using the improved Yellow Cameleon 3.6 (YC3.6) fluorescence reporter [102]. Col-0 and cpk3-1cpk6-1 plants were transformed with YC3.6. Based on calibration measurements, the imposed Ca2+ transients using YC3.6 corresponded to average cytoplasmic Ca2+ baseline levels of approximately 0.15 muM and average peak levels of approximately 0.6 muM. The imposed oscillation protocol that was applied subjects cells to large changes in both the external Ca2+ and Cl- concentrations. Earlier versions of cameleon were sensitive to the Cl- concentration, as Cl- affects the pH sensitivity of the yellow fluorescent protein chromophore [103] and therefore previous studies were performed with yellow cameleon YC2.1 which has important amino acid substitutions (V68L and Q69K) that substantially reduce sensitivity to the interacting Cl- and H+ ions [104,105]. In the present study, YC3.6 was used, which also has important amino acid substitutions that substantially reduce sensitivity to the interacting Cl- and H+ ions and a greatly enhanced ratio changes in response to physiological [Ca2+]cyt changes [102]. Previous work with YC2.1 showed that the ratio changes observed during imposed oscillations are due to the changes in calcium, not changes in Cl-, as imposing the same chloride changes while removing extracellular Ca2+ does not produce any YC2.1 ratio changes (supplemental data to [29]; ). In these experiments, extracellular Ca2+ was chelated with 10 mM EGTA, which lowers external Ca2+ to nanomolar levels, to physically inhibit Ca2+ influx that would otherwise occur at strongly hyperpolarized potentials. In further controls, replacing CaCl2 with MgCl2 in the bath did not produce cameleon ratio changes [106]. Further control experiments were performed with the new reporter YC3.6 in which Ca2+ changes were imposed but not Cl- changes, by using the impermeant counteranion imminodiacetate (Figure 10). Stomata were extracellularly perfused alternately with solutions containing either 100 mM K+ imminodiacetate (no added Ca2+) (pH 6.15) or 1 mM K+ imminodiacetate and 1 mM Ca2+ imminodiacetate (pH 6.15). These controls showed YC3.6 ratio changes in the absence of imposed Cl- changes, demonstrating that Ca2+ changes are being reported (Figure 10), as previously shown for YC2.1 [29,104,105].
###end p 71
###begin title 72
Germination assays.
###end title 72
###begin p 73
###xml 59 62 59 62 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b107">107</xref>
Germination assays were performed as described previously [107]. Mutant and wild-type seeds were harvested at the same time and then sterilized using chlorine. Sterilized seeds were plated on 1/2 MS medium containing MES (0.5 g/L) (pH 5.7), supplemented with 0, 0.3, 1, and 5 muM ABA. Plates were kept in the cold room for 2 d and then transferred to a growth room. Seed germination was scored on days 3, 5, 7, and 11.
###end p 73

###end p 74

###xml 218 220 218 220 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b054">54</xref>
###xml 302 309 302 309 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s2">Results</xref>
###xml 312 318 312 318 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ACTIN2</italic>
###xml 377 381 377 381 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CDPK</italic>
(A) Expression of CPK3 and CPK6 in guard cell (GC) and mesophyll cell (MC) protoplasts was examined by RT-PCR. Control amplifications of the guard cell-expressed KAT1 gene and the mesophyll-expressed CBP marker genes [54] (Leonhardt et al., 2004) were used to test the purity of cell preparations (see Results). ACTIN2 was used for an internal loading control. To amplify each CDPK-specific band, RT-PCR was performed with primer sets as indicated by arrowheads in (B) for 36 cycles. Plants were sprayed with water (-ABA) or 100 muM ABA (+ABA) 4 h before isolation of protoplasts and RNA extraction.
###end p 198
###begin p 199
###xml 53 57 53 57 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk3</italic>
###xml 62 66 62 66 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpk6</italic>
(B) Cartoon showing the T-DNA insertion positions in cpk3 and cpk6 T-DNA insertion alleles. PCR was performed with a left boarder primer of the T-DNA and a gene-specific primer, and the PCR products were sequenced to determine the T-DNA insertion positions. Arrowheads indicate primer locations for RT-PCR in (A) and (C). ATG and TGA indicate start and stop codons. White boxes indicate exons.

###begin title 219

Ca2+-Reactive Closure Is Impaired in cpk3cpk6 Double Mutant Stomata

###xml 117 118 117 118 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">n</italic>

Individually mapped stomatal apertures were measured for the last 30 min before imposed [Ca2+]cyt transients (before Time = 0) and for the ensuing 180 min at the indicated time points. Error bars represent SEM. Inset (top) shows imposed [Ca2+]cyt transients in wild-type (blue trace) and in cpk3-1cpk6-1 (red trace) guard cells expressing Yellow Cameleon 3.6 (R.U.: ratio units).

###begin title 224
###xml 64 68 64 68 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK3</italic>
###xml 73 77 73 77 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK6</italic>
Simplified Models for Early ABA Signal Transduction Network and CPK3 and CPK6 Functions in Guard Cells
###end title 224
###begin p 225
###xml 17 19 17 19 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 48 50 48 50 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 88 90 88 90 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 103 107 103 107 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK3</italic>
###xml 112 116 112 116 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK6</italic>
###xml 128 130 128 130 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 131 134 131 134 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cyt</sub>
###xml 172 176 172 176 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK3</italic>
###xml 181 185 181 185 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK6</italic>
###xml 196 198 196 198 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Ca</sub>
###xml 201 203 201 203 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 326 336 326 336 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s3">Discussion</xref>
###xml 389 398 389 398 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CPK3-CPK6</italic>
###xml 556 558 556 558 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="pbio-0040327-b089">89</xref>
###xml 565 575 565 575 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s3">Discussion</xref>
Plasma membrane ICa channel and intracellular Ca2+-release mechanisms cause cytosolic Ca2+ elevations. CPK3 and CPK6 mediate [Ca2+]cyt activation of S-type anion channels. CPK3 and CPK6 regulate ICa Ca2+ channels by a proposed feedback (A) or parallel pathway (B) or by transcriptional/translational regulation mechanism (see Discussion). R-type anion channels are regulated in a parallel CPK3-CPK6-independent signal transduction pathway. The arrow connecting R-type and S-type anion channels indicates that these channels may share molecular components [89]. See Discussion for details.
###end p 225
###begin title 226
###xml 104 105 104 105 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 158 169 158 169 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Arabidopsis</italic>
###xml 239 241 239 241 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2+</sup>
###xml 260 261 260 261 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
Alterations in the Extracellular Calcium Concentration in the Absence of Changes in the Extracellular Cl- Concentration Cause Large Ratio Changes in YC3.6 in Arabidopsis Guard Cells Illustrating that YC3.6, Like YC2.1, Reports Cytosolic Ca2+ Changes and Not Cl- Changes during Imposed Transients
###end title 226
###begin p 227
###xml 4 25 4 25 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
See Materials and Methods. The YFP/CFP emission ratio is monitored in a guard cell (wild-type) expressing YC3.6. Ratio increases accompany exposure to high extracellular calcium using the membrane-impermeable counteranion, imminodiacetate.
###end p 227
